      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2023/MH/d3mh00982c/d3mh00982c-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3mh00982c-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2023/MH/d3mh00982c/d3mh00982c-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">Cyclic voltammograms (black) and evolution of the film mass (blue) during the third cycle (arrows indicate the scanning direction) for the MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (a), rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O (b) and rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> (c) films. Conditions: Gold/quartz substrate, NaCl electrolyte (0.1 mol L<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and scan rate 10 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">In both the rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7b</a>) and rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7c</a>) samples, there is a similar mass change profile with a steady mass increase starting at 0.0 V (1) and continuing up to 0.4 V for rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O and up to 1.0 V for rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> (2). In fact, the mass change profile of the tri-component material appears to be a mixture between the profiles of MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7a</a>) and rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7b</a>), indicating the contribution of all the materials through the entire process. During oxidation, the mass starts to decrease near 0.3 V (3) and remains constant up to 0.2 V for rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O and 0.6 V for rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> (4). Furthermore, the differences in mass obtained during the CV cycles reveal increases in mass of 8.1, 11.3 and 13.5% for the rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O, MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> films, respectively, indicating that the ternary film has the greatest intercalation capacity for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions, corroborating the EIS data discussed earlier and supporting the performance of this material as electrodes, as will be discussed next.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The performance of the nanoarchitected thin films as anodes for aqueous sodium-ion batteries was analyzed based on the CV profiles of each sample. GCD curves were obtained in 0.1 mol L<small><sup>1</sup></small> aqueous solution of NaCl in the potential window between 0.2 and 0.4 V (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8</a>). Currents of 0.1, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1 and 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (Fig. S21, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) were applied, and the specific capacities (SC) were calculated (<a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a>). <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8a and b</a> displays the GCD profile of the materials operating at a current of 0.1 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The GCD curves exhibit a plateau between 0.1 to 0.2 V, indicating the intercalation of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> in the thin films, as previously shown in the CV curves (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6</a>) and EQCM measurements (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7</a>). <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8c and d</a> show the variation of the specific capacity according the number of CD cycles, demonstrating the decrease in the storage capacity of the materials as the current density increases, which is the expected profile for batteries due to the internal resistance of the materials, which limits the speed at which cations can migrate in and out of the structure.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig8"><a href="/image/article/2023/MH/d3mh00982c/d3mh00982c-f8_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3mh00982c-f8.tif" src="/image/article/2023/MH/d3mh00982c/d3mh00982c-f8.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 8 </b> <span id="fig8"><span class="graphic_title">Charge and discharge curves (a) and (b); specific capacity of the discharge process (c) and (d) at different current densities (0.1, 0.25, 0.5, 0.75, 1 and 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>); specific capacity measured during 200 cycles at 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (e) and Coulombic efficiency (f) of the nanocomposites in 0.1 mol L<small><sup>1</sup></small> NaCl aqueous solution and the potential range of -0.2 to 0.4 V.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>

        <hr class="hrule"><br>
      <p class="otherpara">The MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> film exhibited an impressive SC value (551 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) that was significantly higher than the values obtained for this same film in KCl aqueous solution (276 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit56"><sup><span class="sup_ref">56</span></sup></a> suggesting that hydrated Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> is more easily intercalated than hydrated K<small><sup>+</sup></small>. This high capacity was not retained in the rGO-based MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> binary composites, in which the SC values were 280 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-LbL), 238 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-mixing) and 206 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span>). The SC for the pristine rGO film was not determined, as it does not exhibit a redox process. The copper-oxide-nanoparticlebased materials, however, present impressive electrochemical performance, with rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O having an SC value of 620 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. In addition to the redox process attributed to copper oxide NPs, this result is also explained by the presence of the more-conductive rGO in this sample (due to the more effective reduction of GO to rGO, as discussed earlier), which is expected to improve the electrical double layer. Regarding the nanoarchitected tri-component structures, the findings are particularly noteworthy: (i) rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-LbL presents an SC of 1321 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, which represents a 240%, 213% and 472% increase compared to those of MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O and rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-LbL, respectively; (ii) rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-mixing presents an SC of 1056 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, which is 192%, 170% and 444% higher than those of MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O and rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-mixing, respectively; (iii) rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> presents an impressive SC of 1377 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, which represents a 250%, 222% and 668% increase compared to those of MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O and rGO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> respectively. These data are summarized in <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a>.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">
        <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8e</a> presents the specific capacity measured during 200 charge/discharge cycles at 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> film exhibits instability during the first 50 cycles, which can be attributed to the volume change and structural breakage that occurs in this material during the GCD processes. When MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> is combined with rGO or rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O, greater stability is observed during cycling. In the films generated using rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O, a negligible loss of stability is observed in the initial 10 cycles, which can be ascribed to the adjustment of the CuO/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> in the structure during the process of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> intercalation/de-intercalation. The only film that exhibits a high loss of stability during cycling is the rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-LbL film, in which the contact among the components is not as close as in the other films. The coulombic efficiency of the materials, as determined from 200 charge/discharge cycles (as presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8f</a> and <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a>), ranges between 70% and 90%. The rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-LbL film is an exception, showing low stability as previously discussed. The performance of the rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span> thin film was followed over 1000 consecutive charge/discharge cycles at elevated current (Fig.S22, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), and it demonstrated a stability of 50%.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The SC values of the tri-component films obtained in this study are comparable to the remarkable values reported in the literature. These results are attributed to several factors: (i) the high charge storage capacity of the three materials used in this study; (ii) the improved conductivity achieved through the use of reduced and better-structured graphene; (iii) the formation of nanocomposites that prevent the restacking of 2D materials and accommodate the volume changes of the MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O nanoparticles; (iv) the employment of nanoarchitected structures that possess high surface area and homogeneity; (v) the intrinsic characteristics of each of the tri-component structures obtained in the samples, <span class="italic">e.g.</span>, the small flakes of the few-layer MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the coexistence of Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>O/CuO, and the very small Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O nanoparticles dispersed through the entire sample; and (vi) the synergistic effect among the three components due to the intimate contact among them, which is directly dependent on the preparation method. In the best sample, rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span>, each of the three components is in intimate contact as a result of the nanoarchitected way in which they are structured. The graphene sheets contribute to the overall performance, allowing cation adsorption and playing a crucial role in enhancing the conductivity (as observed by EIS) and the resistance to mechanical stress of both MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O NPs during cycling. The insertion of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> into the electrode occurs through the interaction with the three components, while the excellent electrical conductivity of graphene facilitates efficient charge transfer during the intercalation process, contributing to the overall performance and stability of the electrode.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">
        <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab2">Table 2</a> presents a summarized comparison between the results reported in this work with those using different MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/graphene composites and some ternary combinations (MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/graphene/other) applied to energy storage. The full table is available in the ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> (Table S3). It can be noted that the majority of the data presented in the literature is based on LIBs and organic electrolytes, which makes our results for SIBs in aqueous electrolyte even more impressive. Finally, it is important to point out that this is the first report of a ternary material comprising rGO, MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O nanoparticles prepared as a thin and transparent film. Similar ternary combinations have been reported only in two very recent papers by Selvamani <span class="italic">et al.</span> (2020)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit118"><sup><span class="sup_ref">118</span></sup></a> and (2021),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit119"><sup><span class="sup_ref">119</span></sup></a> which were prepared as powders for alkaline supercapacitor applications.</p>

        <hr class="hrule"><br>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect1610"><span class="a_heading">4. Conclusion</span></h2>
      <span>The results presented and discussed in this work represent significant advances in the search for novel electrode materials for aqueous sodium ion batteries. The superlative performance of ternary materials specifically designed for this application was demonstrated for the first time, in which the individual response of each component was synergistically potentiated by the unique nanoarchitected structure in which the materials were prepared. Equally relevantly, the potential of immiscible liquid interfaces to both prepare and process sophisticated materials in a controlled way has also been demonstrated. None of the widely known techniques for thin film deposition could be used to prepare graphene/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>/copper oxide nanoparticle tri-component thin films materials like those reported here. However, through the wide range of experimental variations provided by LLIR, three ternary films have been obtained, in which the specific interactions among the components, and consequently the electrochemical response of the final materials, could be controlled.</span>
      <p class="otherpara">The remarkable architectures of these materials place them among the best reported so far for use as electrodes in aqueous sodium-ion batteries. Faradaic mechanisms due to MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Cu<small><sub>2</sub></small>O/CuO have been observed and identified in the three-component films, while graphene improves the conductivity and makes a non-faradaic contribution to the electrode capacity. The insertion/de-insertion of cations into the electrodes was followed using a quartz microbalance and found to coincide with the charge changes. These ternary materials demonstrate notable specific capacity enhancements, ranging from 200% to 600% in comparison to their respective control films. The best results, with a specific capacity of 1377 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and a recovery rate of 100%, were obtained for the sample rGO/Cu<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>O/MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>-<span class="italic">in situ</span>, which is the sample that was prepared with the best, most-improved and most-intimate interactions among the components.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Finally, it is important to note that the unique nanostructures of the ternary materials presented here make them promising candidates for several other technological applications, such as electrochemical sensors or catalysts. Also, the ease with which the films can be deposited over ordinary substrates, such as plastics, will enable their use in flexible devices, and the high optical quality exhibited by these films opens great avenues toward applications in which transparency is required, such as optical devices, photovoltaics and transparent batteries.</p>

            <br><a href="https://cookiepedia.co.uk/giving-consent-to-cookies" class="privacy-notice-link" rel="noopener" target="_blank" aria-label="More information about your privacy, opens in a new tab">More information</a></div><button id="accept-recommended-btn-handler">Allow all</button><section class="ot-sdk-row ot-cat-grp"><h3 id="ot-category-title"> Manage consent preferences</h3><div class="ot-pli-hdr ot-leg-border-color"><span class="ot-li-title">Consent</span> <span class="ot-li-title">Legitimate interest</span></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0001"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0001" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0001 ot-status-id-C0001"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0001">Strictly necessary cookies</h4></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0001">These cookies are necessary for the website to function and cannot be switched off in our systems. They are usually only set in response to actions made by you which amount to a request for services, such as setting your privacy preferences, logging in or filling in forms. You can set your browser to block or alert you about these cookies, but some parts of the site will not then work. These cookies do not store any personally identifiable information.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0002"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0002">Analytical cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0002" id="ot-group-id-C0002" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0002"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Analytical cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0002">These cookies allow us to count visits and traffic sources so we can measure and improve the performance of our site. They help us to know which pages are the most and least popular and see how visitors move around the site. All information these cookies collect is aggregated and therefore anonymous. If you do not allow these cookies we will not know when you have visited our site, and will not be able to monitor its performance.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0003"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0003">Functional cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0003" id="ot-group-id-C0003" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0003"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Functional cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0003">These cookies enable the website to provide enhanced functionality and personalisation. They may be set by us or by third party providers whose services we have added to our pages. If you do not allow these cookies then some or all of these services may not function properly.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0004"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0004" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0004"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0004">Targeting cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0004" id="ot-group-id-C0004" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0004" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0004"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0004"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Targeting cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0004">These cookies may be set through our site by our advertising partners.
